Loose flock of 5 robin-sized birds moving from brush to brush southwards along the trail. Solid identification of 2 birds as Varied Thrush. Unambiguous head pattern of the Varied Thrush - orange stripe above the eye and orange throat, orange breast, mostly dark back.  The other three presumed to be the same since they were traveling together. Difficult viewing conditions, as we were walking into the low (winter) sun and the birds were ahead of us and moving in that direction, so when they flew from tree to tree they were backlit. The flock was moving south, keeping well ahead of us, for about 1/4 mile, and we lost sight of them at about where the Tahoe Rim Trail crosses the spring-fed stream that seems to always be flowing, and was still flowing today (partly frozen) in spite of the drought. --  We turned around three miles from the trailhead, at the overlook before the trail starts losing elevation. On the way back we again saw a flock of 5 robin-sized birds, at about 12:00 noon. Again they were well ahead of us, but I did manage to get a photo of one that, while poor, is unambiguous in verifying that it is a Varied Thrush. We assume it was the same flock. This time, it was about a mile from the trailhead, just south of the first broad overlook of Lake Tahoe, about a mile north of the first sighting.
